League of Nations Meeting Tomorrow: Sanctions Against Italy to be Maintained; British Public Opinion Firmly States That the League Secretariat Also Declares the Status of Abyssinia Remains Unchanged 58

(London) Viscount Cecil stated in a speech at the League of Nations Association meeting today that the League must maintain sanctions against Italy, and even intensify them if necessary. Ten thousand listeners cheered in unison.

Cecil continued, saying that the British people had not been so moved since the death of General Gordon. The Emperor of Abyssinia is a true hero, willing to go into exile rather than accept dishonorable treatment after being betrayed by those he trusted. As long as there is a glimmer of hope, the British people cannot recognize any other government in Abyssinia. Abyssinia remains a member of the League of Nations and is entitled to the collective protection it has been promised. Subsequently, Attlee, the leader of the Labor Party (opposition party) in the House of Commons, proposed a resolution declaring support for the League of Nations and the principle of collective security, expressing indignation at the invasion of Abyssinia, and urging the British government to maintain sanctions until Italy is prepared to accept peace terms recognized by the League of Nations. The resolution was passed unanimously amidst great excitement. (Reuters, 8th)

(London) With the League of Nations Council meeting approaching, the British attitude towards the sanctions issue urgently needs to be discussed with the governments of the various Dominions in order to determine a policy. Foreign Secretary Eden recently convened a meeting with Sir James Parr, the High Commissioner of New Zealand in the United Kingdom; Bruce, the High Commissioner of Australia; Waterson, the High Commissioner of South Africa; and Massey, the High Commissioner of Canada, to discuss this issue. It is reported that each of these High Commissioners stated that if the Italo-Abyssinian dispute cannot be resolved within the framework of the League of Nations, their respective Dominion governments would firmly oppose the abolition of sanctions. (Havas, 8th)

(London) Political figures believe that at the upcoming session of the League of Nations Council, a resolution will likely be passed stating that a solution is only appropriate if it is deemed acceptable by the League of Nations, and the discussion of a solution will be postponed until the next session. This would not cause any dissent in Britain. However, if Italy were to declare the annexation of Abyssinia before the Council session, the stance adopted by Britain would completely change, possibly becoming more assertive. (Havas, 8th)

(London) All British morning newspapers anticipate that the League of Nations Council meeting on Monday will not take any drastic steps regarding the Abyssinian issue and will adjourn. In other words, the current sanctions against Italy will continue in their current form. Italian Army Administers Administration in the Abyssinian Capital; Difficult Situation for Foreign Embassies 62

Addis Ababa: The Italian army is currently handling the restoration of administrative work in Addis Ababa, having divided the entire city into four districts, each with a general office. Each has 30 border guards in customs guard uniforms and 70 inspectors. The inspectors are currently searching for stolen goods house by house and arresting those who are hiding them. The chief inspector is currently receiving various weapons, such as knives, swords, guns, etc., voluntarily surrendered by Abyssinians at the city hall, while the lower level of the city hall is detaining Abyssinians of various ages and appearances awaiting trial, most of whom are only accused of theft. It is not thought that they will be severely punished, but the detainees either do not admit to robbery or claim that what they are carrying is their own property, so it is difficult for the inspectors to determine their guilt. (Reuters, 9th)

Addis Ababa: After being guarded for several days by 30 Askaris soldiers carrying old-fashioned 1890 rifles, the manager of the Bank of Abyssinia, Wright, has reached an agreement with the Italian authorities on the method of reopening the bank today. The bank's funds, amounting to 1.5 million thalers (Abyssinian currency), are said to be under the control of the Italian authorities. The large store opened by British Indian Muhammad Ali has been preserved intact due to the protection of the British Embassy's Indian troops. It is now crowded with customers, and the inventory may be sold out today. US Senate Passes Naval Budget, Sent to House of Representatives for Approval 70

(Washington) The Senate today passed a naval budget of $529,000,000 to build two battleships. It also stipulates the expenditure to build 18 smaller warships, 333 aircraft, and increase naval personnel to 100,000 men. The Marine Corps will be increased to 17,000 men. The bill has now been returned to the House for reconsideration. (National News Agency, 8th)

(Washington) The Senate today passed a naval bill providing for an expenditure of $531,000,000 in order to:

* Continue the construction of 84 warships currently underway.

* Build 16 new destroyers and 6 new submarines.

* Increase naval aviation equipment.

* Stockpile mineral products for wartime needs.

* Build two new battleships if other countries begin to replace their capital ships.

Before passing the bill, the Senate rejected a motion by Republican Frazier by a vote of 40 to 12 to delete the provision for building two battleships, six submarines, and twelve destroyers at a cost of $153,000,000. Frazier stated that the bill was completely contrary to the Kellogg-Briand Pact. "Do we want peace or war? That is the question," he said. This bill will ensure that the US Navy is not inferior to other countries. It has now been returned to the House along with Senate amendments. The aforementioned two battleships must wait until other signatory countries of the London Naval Treaty build capital ships before construction can begin. President Roosevelt stated today that he will submit the London Naval Treaty to Congress in the middle of next week. Senator Pittman, Chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, stated that the Foreign Relations Committee will begin reviewing the treaty next Saturday or Sunday. He could not predict whether the treaty would be approved during this session of Congress, as the matter depends on the legislative situation. (Reuters, 8th)

Hindenburg Airship Arrives in New York from Germany in 62 Hours 71

Lakehurst, New Jersey: The world's largest airship, the Hindenburg, departed from its base in Friedrichshafen, Germany, at 9:30 AM on Thursday for a flight across the North Atlantic to the United States. It arrived here safely at 6:10 AM this morning (local time), making the flight in 61 hours and 40 minutes, setting a new airship record. Thousands of New Jersey residents got up early to eagerly welcome the airship, and hundreds more gathered on the tops of tall buildings to wait for it overnight. The airship flew within a few hundred feet of the tops of tall buildings, so the crowds could see it very clearly. The airship mistook another mast for the mast designated to stop the airship and was in great danger when its bow approached it. The chosen mast had hundreds of soldiers standing below it to grab the descending mooring ropes, but this location had none. The field officer hesitated for a moment, unsure whether to signal the airship to fly upward quickly, but then suddenly had a flash of inspiration and shouted for some of the reporters and other personnel on the field to grab the ropes. The airship came to a safe stop only after this. (Reuters, 9th)

From the Hindenburg Airship: The Hindenburg airship crossed the Atlantic today, encountering favorable winds and flying very fast. It is expected to fly over New York City on Saturday morning. The captain plans to make the New England coast the first landing point in the United States. (National News Agency, 8th)

Educational Broadcasting Special Edition

Chemistry Lecture Series 1: The Teaching of Chemistry in Secondary Schools (Part 2) 75

— Chen Kezhong, Full-time Translator, National Compilation and Translation Bureau

Third, regarding experiments, we should develop habits of cleanliness, agility, and caution. As mentioned earlier, chemistry is an experimental science. Without experiments and observations, we cannot talk about chemistry. Therefore, experiments are extremely important for students' progress. To conduct experiments, we must cultivate habits of cleanliness, agility, and caution, because if we are not clean, we often cannot obtain correct results. Once upon a time, there was a famous German chemist, V. Meyer. Once, when he was lecturing on the blue reaction of benzene and isatin, he performed an experiment on the spot for the students to see. As a result, he failed repeatedly. He had tried it successfully beforehand, but when he demonstrated it, it suddenly failed. Later, his assistant told him that the benzene used in the past was extracted from coal tar, but the benzene used this time was made in the laboratory from other substances. The benzene extracted from coal tar contains impurities. The benzene made in the laboratory is pure. The previous blue reaction was not a reaction of benzene, but a reaction of its impurities. From this, it can be seen that impure reagents will definitely affect the experimental results. If people who do chemistry experiments do not develop clean habits, these incorrect results will occur at any time. However, Meyer was a first-class chemist. Later, he used this error to study why impure benzene can produce a blue reaction with isatin. As a result, he discovered thiophene. As for agility, it is of course a very important habit, because agility represents your proficiency. Only when your procedure is proficient can you get satisfactory results. This is the proverb, "practice makes perfect." As for caution, it should be paid attention to, because if you are not careful, not only will the experiment often fail, but there is also the possibility of danger. For example, recently, a chemistry professor at Guangxi University, who was very experienced in the study of explosives, was experimenting with a large amount of explosives one day. His wife happened to come to the laboratory to see him. When he turned his head, he accidentally dropped the explosives on the ground and they exploded, killing him and seriously injuring his wife. It is inappropriate to use such a large amount of explosives for experiments. However, this professor relied on his extensive experience and thought there would be no problem. As a result, he suffered a tragic death. Even an experienced chemistry professor like him suffered such a tragic result due to occasional negligence. Then, of course, beginners should be more cautious about all experiments.

Regarding the attitude that should be taken when learning chemistry, first, we should have a desire for knowledge. Chemistry is not only closely related to people's food, clothing, housing, and transportation, but it can also be used to discover the mysteries of nature. Facts that were once regarded as mysterious can now be slowly discovered using chemical methods. For example, in terms of products, many things can not only be manufactured artificially, but the products made are much better than natural products. Many important chemical inventions almost all come from the "desire for knowledge" of chemists. A person with a desire for knowledge will be interested in what they learn and will not become discouraged when they encounter difficulties, but will seek deep understanding. Chemistry is the key to exploring the mysterious facts of nature, and only those who are extremely eager for knowledge can grasp this key. If we want to have considerable success in chemistry, we should pay attention to cultivating this desire for knowledge.

Second, we should develop habits of realism and precision. Everyone agrees that people who study should be realistic, but why do we emphasize the word precision? People who are new to chemistry may not all understand. Now I will give an example, and you will know why people who study chemistry cannot help but develop precise habits. In 1785, when Cavendish measured the composition of air, he mixed ordinary air with oxygen and then passed electricity through it to completely remove the nitrogen in the air by combining with oxygen. Although he tried many times, there was always a small amount of gas in the bottle that could not be removed. He thought that this little gas had little impact on the study of air composition, so he ignored it. A hundred years later, this small amount of gas was painstakingly studied by two chemists, Rayleigh and Ramsey, and as a result, the argon group of rare gases was discovered. To give another example: The great German organic chemist Liebig once had a factory send someone to ask him to analyze a kind of red liquid. He did not carefully examine it and concluded that the liquid was a mixture of chlorine and iodine. Later, the French chemist Balard discovered bromine, and this new element was the same thing as the red liquid that Liebig had. He greatly regretted that he should not have been so careless and deceived himself. These facts can prove that people who study chemistry should develop precise habits.

Third, we should have a firm spirit. The content of chemistry is complex and the scope is also very broad. It is not an easy science to learn. Especially when you are a beginner, you often feel overwhelmed when you see many formulas, theorems, and definitions. But if you can deal with it with a firm and courageous spirit, then you will not be discouraged when you encounter difficulties and will not achieve anything in your life. The famous German chemist Baeyer spent many years studying the structure of indigo before he succeeded. This kind of firm spirit is very admirable and worthy of our imitation.

Fourth, we should have independent habits. To learn chemistry well, it all depends on the students themselves. Whether the knowledge comes from teachers or books, if you do not carefully consider it with your own mind, you cannot have a deep understanding, and what you have learned cannot be considered your own knowledge. Although the knowledge gained from lectures or books can be said to be delicious food, if it is not digested by ourselves, then it will not benefit us. As for doing chemistry experiments, it is even more necessary to have independent habits. Needless to say, everything in the experiment must be done with your own hands. You must also carefully observe the various phenomena produced by the experiment and write them down in your own words, so that you can make real progress. Therefore, independent habits should also be cultivated. Some students like to copy other people's results when doing experiments. This is the worst habit and should be reformed.

Although there are many shortcomings in chemistry education in the past, there have been practical improvements recently. Therefore, chemistry education can be said to have reached a new stage. The above-mentioned improvement methods are just an outline for the education authorities. On the one hand, we must rely on the cooperation of middle school teachers and textbook editors across the country. On the other hand, we must also rely on middle school students across the country to work hard with a spirit of seeking truth in chemistry. Then, middle school chemistry education can have real hope for development. (End)

Ministry of Finance Sends Personnel to Investigate Smuggling in North China, All Kinds of Tax Revenues are Reduced, Smuggling Suppression Methods Need to Be Improved 76

Tianjin Correspondence: The serious situation of smuggling in North China has not yet been resolved. In reality, it involves various diplomatic issues and is not easy to eradicate in a short period of time. The Japanese side has great ambitions for tax revenues in North China. Smuggling is only one of its policies, using this to create an extraordinary state in North China. It cannot be stopped by mere words. The Hebei-Chahar authorities, according to the instructions of the central government, are still ordering Xiao Zhenying and Lin Shize to do their best to negotiate with the Japanese side. If they can obtain a glimmer of hope, it will be enough to plug a hole. Therefore, the current negotiations are still in progress. Since the Tianjin Customs implemented armed anti-smuggling at the Lao Tieshan Cape in the Bohai Bay, on the 6th of this month, it continued to intercept five smuggling steamships operated by Japanese ruffians near Qikou. There was a sensation at the time and a conflict occurred, but the ships were eventually detained by patrol boats. The ships arrived in Tianjin on the 7th, and the cargo, which included rayon, sugar, and seafood totaling more than 3,000 tons, has been confiscated. The Japanese Consul in Tianjin, Nagai, specifically visited Xu Lier, the Acting Inspector General of Customs, to protest this matter and demand the return of the ships and cargo. Negotiations have not yet been completed. It is heard that the Customs has expressed that it can return a small amount of the fines for the ships. However, due to the double difficulties of being located in the pseudo-East Hebei Inspection Office and smuggling by Japanese ruffians, any anti-smuggling methods are not easy to be effective in Qinhuangdao's seafood. On the 5th of this month, two customs officers were injured on the seashore of Liushouwangying. Fortunately, the security team under Zhang Yantian arrived and used force to disperse the Japanese ruffians, rescuing the customs officers. The ships and cargo were able to sail to the Qinhuangdao Customs pier to dock and be dealt with. The Ministry of Finance is paying close attention to the rampant smuggling in North China. The personnel dispatched recently arrived in Tianjin. In the past two days, they visited Mayor Xiao Zhenying, Tianjin Customs Superintendent Lin Shize, and Changlu Salt Commissioner Ge Dingyuan to inquire about the actual situation, so as to plan a perfect strategy. After staying in Tianjin for a week, Xiao will go to Baoding and then transfer to the four provinces of Chahar, Shanxi, Suiyuan, and Henan to investigate. He will return to Beijing at the end of the month to report. According to someone, this time he was ordered to come north, first to Beiping, to investigate the silk tax bureaus of the four provinces of Hebei, Shanxi, Chahar, and Suiyuan, and the tobacco and alcohol stamp tax bureau of Hebei Province. The unified tax of the four provinces has decreased by several million yuan due to smuggling. This time he came to Tianjin to investigate customs and salt taxes, and to pay attention to whether the competent authorities have fulfilled their responsibilities, so that he can report to the ministry for correction. The loss of customs duties due to rampant smuggling is very large. The ministry regards this as a part of the entire diplomatic situation and will seek an overall solution from the diplomatic aspect. Regarding the salt tax, due to environmental influences, the tax revenue in the Changlu area is not good. In order to rectify the national salt affairs, the central government has decided to implement the new salt law from the next year. It is heard that the old system of drawing boundaries will be completely broken, and people can freely sell and eat salt, free from multiple layers of exploitation, and salt tax revenue can also be more prosperous. As for the production of Lu salt, the ministry has ordered the Changlu Transport Office to handle it. For anti-smuggling in North China, because most of the smugglers belong to a certain country, earnestly investigating them is prone to disputes. Only by cracking down on profiteering merchants and assisting the chamber of commerce may be effective. He has already contacted the person in charge of the chamber of commerce in Beiping to discuss this matter, hoping that they will work hard. Upon arriving in Tianjin, he also conveyed the ministry's intentions. (9th)

Tada Talks Extensively About New Sino-Japanese Goodwill, Holds Farewell Reception for Chinese and Foreign Dignitaries in Peiping, Scheduled to Return to His Country on the 24th to Assume New Position 77

Peiping Correspondence: Lieutenant General Tada Shun, Commander of the Japanese Garrison in Tianjin, has been transferred to become the Commander of the 11th Division and is scheduled to return to his country on the 24th of this month to take up his new post. On the 7th, he came to Peiping to host a tea party for Chinese and foreign dignitaries in Peiping as a farewell. On the 8th, he went by car to Tongxian to visit the pseudo-Eastern Hebei authorities, where Yin Rugeng prepared lunch to entertain him. Tada stayed in Tongxian to receive members, taking a chartered car prepared by the Beining Railway and attached to the Peiping express train to return to Tianjin. Qin Dechun, Shao Wenkai, Pan Yugui, Chen Zhongfu, Lin Gengyu, Lan Gongshi Xiaoliang, Hamada, Shimizu, Watanabe, and Nichihashi, as well as the Peiping Public Security Bureau Security Team band, went to the station to see him off. The following is a record of Tada's conversation with reporters before his departure: "I have now been transferred to the position of division commander and will soon return to my country, so I have nothing to say. I only hope that the general public of your country can live and work in peace and contentment, truly achieving co-existence and co-prosperity between the people of China and Japan. This is not only my personal hope, but also the hope of the general public of Japan."

"My impression of being in China is that many places in your country misunderstand the intentions of Japan and the garrison, leading to the misunderstanding that Japan is creating trouble out of thin air, taking the opportunity to invade China, and hindering China's unification efforts. The Empire is determined to eliminate this kind of thinking. Taking a family as an example, even parents and children should have the virtue of humility, let alone two countries. If the two countries do not yield to each other, it will be difficult to achieve true friendship. As for the two countries, they should help each other with their strengths and make up for their own shortcomings. Only by being kind and yielding to each other can there be success."

"During the Tang and Song dynasties, Japan had Chinese students who brought back a lot of Chinese culture and instilled it in the minds of the general public. This was taking the strengths of your country to make up for the weaknesses of our country. Now, Japanese culture is stronger than Chinese culture, and your country can also make use of Japan. China is a large country in East Asia and should cooperate with all its strength in order to maintain peace in East Asia. As for the extent to which Japanese culture has progressed, I hope you will visit our country to see for yourselves. You will know that the Japanese people have no ill feelings towards China, and you can also see that Japanese culture has reached an unimaginable level. If you want to go to our country, our country is willing to help you. The military attache Imai in Peiping and Major General Komuro can all be contacted. As the saying goes, seeing is believing. If you go to Japan, you will know what Japan hopes for from China and you can dispel all misunderstandings. I have now been transferred to Shikoku, which is a relatively large island in Japan with beautiful scenery. I hope you will visit it when you go to Japan in the future. I am willing to fulfill my responsibility as a guide."

"The Communist Party is the common enemy of China and Japan. I hope that the two countries can work together to repel communism and the Communist Party. The bandits' arrival in North China has had a great impact, which is quite noteworthy to us. Recently, the Communist bandits who entered Shanxi have now left the province, which is a gratifying thing. If the Communist bandits attack Outer Mongolia to the north, the problem will be serious."

"The smuggling problem in North China refers to goods imported from the coast of Eastern Hebei. The goods imported from the coast of Eastern Hebei have already paid a quarter of the tax in accordance with the 'Eastern Hebei' regulations and cannot be considered smuggling. If the Chinese government lowers tariffs, smuggling can be avoided." From this, it can be seen that the other side is using smuggling to coerce our country into lowering tariffs. The reason is very clear. Tada also said that he had not heard of any concrete plans regarding Sino-Japanese economic cooperation, or the extent to which he had contacted the Economic Committee. However, he expected that this matter was still under research and negotiation. "Today I am going to Tongxian for only one hour, so I have no impressions or thoughts." (8th)

Relief Through Labor Road Construction in Xuzhou District, Gathering 2,500 Disaster-Stricken Workers, Funded by the International Famine Relief Commission 78

Xuzhou Correspondence: Relief through labor for the Yellow River disaster in Xuzhou District. The provincial government allocated funds to repair the Wei Lake Dam, and the China International Famine Relief Commission also allocated funds to repair the highways in Xuzhou District, recruiting disaster-stricken workers to provide relief through labor. The commission allocated a total of 40,000 yuan for this project and sent Chief Engineer Baker to Xuzhou for inspection. Initially, it was proposed to repair the embankments, but because the Yellow River water had not receded and the embankment repair project was too large, with limited funds, it was changed to repairing the highways. After Baker's survey, he sent Zhang Jichun to Xuzhou to supervise the repair, and Pastor Peng Yongen, stationed in Xuzhou, presided over the work, gathering 2,500 disaster-stricken workers to repair five highways and one ring road: The Tongpei Road, from the north of the city to Pingshankou, is 50 li long. The entire road from the north of the city to Pingshankou is a gravel road. It will cost 15,000 yuan to add a flat road to the mountain pass. The Guanshan project will also cost 4,000 yuan, making it the most labor-intensive of the roads to be repaired. The Tongqiao Road, from the south of the city to Liangshankou, is 30 li long. The entire road, built with sand mixed with earth by Jing Fanni, is 30 li long and will cost 1,300 yuan. The Tongxiao Road, from the west of the city to Yaolou, is 30 li long. It has always been well-managed and has not been severely damaged, requiring only minor repairs and costing little. The Tongsux Road, from the south of the city to Sanguanmiao, is 10 li long. The route is shorter and will not cost much. As for the ring road, it is being repaired and connected and is now completed. The disaster-stricken workers employed are all recruited from along the banks of Wei Lake, gathering strong men and the elderly alike to provide relief. Each worker is paid 2 to 3 jiao. Each road surface is 12 meters wide, allowing cars and ox carts to pass, with separate lanes for upstream and downstream traffic. All work is expected to be completed by the end of this month, at which time it will be inspected and accepted by the provincial government. (May 6)

Rich Mineral Deposits in Southern Anhui, It is Proposed to Improve Iron Smelting in Counties such as Liu'an, Stibnite in Xiuning and Western Anhui Contains 70% Antimony 79

Wuhu Correspondence: Anhui Province is known throughout the country for its rich production of rice and grain, but it is not widely known that southern Anhui is mountainous and contains countless mineral resources. Unfortunately, due to the changing times, no one has paid attention to them. For example, the annual production of bamboo and wood in Jingxian and Xuancheng is enormous, with the raw materials being transported and sold outside the province. The value of the processed bamboo shoots and Xuan paper is even more considerable, which is clear evidence. In recent years, the Ministry of Industry and the Anhui Provincial Government have paid much attention to southern Anhui and have repeatedly dispatched technical experts to conduct inspections. The Anhui Construction Department has established a Mining Survey Team and a Geology and Mineral Resources Department. However, due to insufficient funds from the provincial government, the above organizations could not be maintained for long. After the determination of the construction plan for the 25th year of the Republic, it was generally believed that it was necessary to re-establish them and actively carry out the work. It has been decided that the coal mines in the northern townships of Guangde County, such as Daxiao Niutoushan, are all high-quality bituminous coal with thick coal seams and abundant reserves. They have been taken over by the province as official mines and will be mined in accordance with the law after obtaining a license. (2) An area of the Huolonggang coal mine in Wuhu County, which was originally contracted by the Huaxing Company, has now been shut down. It has been decided to recruit other merchants to contract it to avoid abandonment. (3) Last year, an area of tin mine was discovered at Dadagang in Xixian County. It is planned to apply for a prospecting license in accordance with the law and conduct exploration. (4) Taihu, Qianshan, Liu'an, and Lihuang counties have historically produced iron sand. Local residents have long used native furnaces to smelt iron and make various utensils, which have been widely sold and can suppress foreign goods. It has been decided to find ways to improve the smelting process to increase production. (5) The stibnite mines in Xishangxikou Ligangshan area of Huizhou Prefecture's Xiuning County have been repeatedly verified by Ding Yi and other investigators from the Industrial Experimentation Institute, containing 68% to 70% antimony, and the quantity is extremely large, which can be mined for 40 years. The Construction Department has obtained a license from the ministry and plans to invite merchants to jointly operate with the government. The extension of the Jiangnan Railway will take the mine area route to facilitate transportation. (May 8)

Travelogue of Qinghai (Continued) 80

— Zhuang Xueben

(3) Qunke Beach Mongolian Banner

One Night in a Black Tent

After crossing another layer of mountain slopes, we reached our destination - Qunke Beach. A dozen or so tents were stationed in the mountain gully, interspersed with two white circular yurts. They were separated from each other by a great distance. The guide led us to dismount in front of a black tent near the yurt. This place was forty li away from Baiyang Gorge, and the pointer on the barometer stopped at 3260 meters.

A woman wearing a pointed hat came out of the tent, held back the large sheepdog, and an old man pulled up the curtain to let us in. I sat down on a velvet flower cushion on the left side of the stove, and the old man also came in with a smile. He was the local Wang, Erlike Beile - Linqin Hujiu Zhajile. His simple attire (wearing an ordinary old sheepskin coat) almost made us mistake him for an ordinary commoner.

We decided to stay here tonight, and the Ula (messenger horses) were sent back. The afternoon's strong wind had long been roaring on the cotton-candy tent top, and the wooden poles supporting the tent were blown down from time to time.

At this time, we were being entertained by the Wang, sitting down by the stove drinking fragrant and salty milk tea. In the wooden box in front of us, there was a grid of ghee (butter), a grid of curds, and a grid of tsampa (roasted barley flour), as well as a plate of freshly boiled blood-water beef taken from the steaming pot (large pieces of half-cooked beef still dripping with blood), which we were free to enjoy.

After drinking tea, we talked about the life, history, religion, and everything else of the Mongolians. However, their Chinese was not very fluent, and none of us understood Mongolian, so when the two sides could not express themselves, the police used tea language to replace it.

The Wang also took out a phonograph from his yurt. Now, although they had the machine, they didn't know how to turn it on and play it, because his son had already gone to Xining. We started to wind up the spring and played a few records, but they were tired of this kind of entertainment.

In the evening, the wind subsided a little, and the yaks on the eastern mountain and the sheep on the western mountain were driven back by the shepherds. They were all busy for a while, surrounding the sheep and tethering the yaks before preparing their dinner. Today, because there were guests, his intelligent new daughter-in-law took the initiative to make a noodle dish that the Han people often eat, cooking a fishy and salty soup noodle with blood-water beef soup.

At night, we unfolded the canvas marching bed where we were sitting. They had never seen it before and looked at it with surprise under the bed. In the dark night, the embers in the stove spat out bright sparks, illuminating the four corners of the tent. Our candles, on the other hand, swayed without light.

The Wang's female relatives and the Wang went to sleep in the yurt to avoid strangers. In the dark tent, only the three of us and the police, two lamas, and an uncle (the Wang's steward) were left. We chatted by the fire for a while and then went to sleep on the left and right sides of the guests and hosts.

The wind at night was even more violent than during the day. Tiny gusts of wind drilled into the tent through the felt, and a piece of black felt was patched over the window seam on top of the cotton candy. The temperature inside the tent had dropped to minus twelve degrees. The sparks in the stove were also gradually diminishing. The roaring storm made the curtain jump and boom, as if it was about to break free from the shackles and fly away. I covered myself with the quilt and went to sleep, but my feet did not feel warm all night. In my dream, I was awakened from time to time by the howling wind outside the cotton candy. At this time, I felt the severity and greatness of the darkness even more.

When I got up the next morning at dawn, the outside of the tent was covered in white snow. The whistling wind had not subsided at all, and the snow was still falling.

Erlike Beile

Chief Erlike Beile is the Prince of the Right Wing Tou Banner of the "Choros Tribe", and is now over sixty years old. He has two pigtails on his upper lip, and his nasal tubes were damaged in his childhood. He speaks entirely with a humming nasal tone, otherwise he could speak a few sentences of Chinese.

He is an enlightened old Wang, who has been to Beijing seven times, twice during the Qing Dynasty. Therefore, although he lives in a grass mountain tent, he is very familiar with the situation outside. His wife has also been to Beijing seven times, so she is now a virtuous woman.

In the early years of the Republic of China, he received the Second Class Medal from President Li Yuanhong. In the twentieth year of the Republic of China, the Mongolian flag organization in Qinghai slightly changed, and he was appointed as the Right Wing Zhengmeng Chief. Now he has the power to command the twelve banners in eastern Qinghai, but there are very few people in his own banner. There are only seventy tents grazing in this area, and only a little more than a hundred in total, including "Baiyang Gorge" and "Qiabuqia". His grazing land was originally in "Qiabuqia" in "Shang Guomi" in Hainan. Recently, due to the migration of Tibetans, his grazing land has shrunk. He has been stationed in Zhouhong here for fifty years. Zhouhong is the pasture of the "Qunke Wang" and is still borrowed from the Qunke Wang.)

His family includes two Taijis (princes), who are currently studying at the Ningmeng Tibetan School, a daughter, a daughter-in-law, a wife, an uncle (steward), two male and female slaves, a cow herder (cowherd boy), and a lama.

His property includes 600 sheep, 200 cattle, 60 horses, two yurts, a black tent, and his yamen in Zhazang Temple.

Mongolian Dress

For those who first arrive in Qinghai, it is difficult to distinguish between the dress of the Mongolian and Tibetan ethnic groups, and they often mistakenly point to the Mongolians. Indeed, this is because there are few differences in their clothing, but if you pay attention, you can also find some significant differences on their bodies. As for the reasons why their clothing is similar, it is said that in recent times, the Tibetan forces in Qinghai have become stronger and the Mongolian forces have gradually declined, so the clothing style has become Tibetanized, and even the language and writing tend to be Tibetan.

The dress of the women here often consists of a round-collared old sheepskin coat, with no lining and a two-inch wide red edge around the edges, with the hem reaching the ground. The rich use purple, blue, or black satin or cloth facings, and a red belt is tied around the waist. On the left side of the body hangs a four-inch long milk hook (a copper hook for milking cows) and a chicken heart-shaped silver plate, which is mostly engraved with flowers and inlaid with gemstones. There are two types of hats: one is a fur ear hat, with two ear flaps on the left and right sides that can be folded down in cold weather, and a large red knot on the top of the hat, with a braid of thread tassels attached; the other is a pointed lambskin hat, with a black wool top and a red circle around the bottom, sewn with a circle of white lambskin. It looks like a hot pot when worn on the head. The top of the hat's wool peak (half of it is decorated with a very delicate bright red tassel, which is the point that differs from the Tibetan dress. Their hair is divided into two strands from the top of the head, drooping from the ears to the chest, and bound with a two-inch wide and three-foot long country flower braid, tied in the middle of the waistband, and the braid still floats down to the ground. Their hairstyle is very different from the braids of Tibetan women that drag on the back, but many young girls who have not yet reached the age of maturity often comb small braids and spread them behind their backs. Their lower bodies may not wear pants for the sake of convenience, and they are accustomed to wearing a kind of hard-soled boots made of cowhide with bare feet.

Men's outerwear is an old sheepskin coat, with pants and hard-soled boots. Hats can be pointed hats, and the wealthy wear fox fur hats. Men's sheepskin coats are mostly raised to below the knees to facilitate riding. Most Mongolians also keep long hair on the top of their heads and comb it into a half-foot long thin braid, coiled in the hat.

Mongolian Life

The life of the Mongolians in Jike Beach is still stagnant in a nomadic society, with no fixed abode, moving with the water and grass. Women's work is often more diligent than men's. Men and women, except for external exchanges or military wars, stay idle in the cotton candy. Women have to milk cows, boil tea, and cook meat in the morning and evening, and take care of household chores in their spare time.

Their diet is based on beef, mutton, ghee, tsampa, curds, and tea. They usually eat three meals a day, and drink more than they eat. Each meal must be accompanied by several bowls of thick juice brewed from brick tea, mixed with a few spoonfuls of fresh milk, ghee, tsampa, and curds. After drinking the tea, they take a bowl of tsampa, mix it with tea and ghee, and knead it into fist-sized dough balls, which is the formal meal. They also eat a lot of beef and mutton from time to time, but the meat is boiled into half-cooked blood-water meat, which outsiders think is unpalatable, but they think it is not delicious without it.

Their residences are either black tents or yurts, because they are easy to disassemble and move. There are more black tents than yurts in this area, which is also due to the influence of Tibetanization. Yurts are made of sheep's wool felt, with ribs made of forest strips inside, forming a conical-shaped tent. It is usually one zhang in diameter, and a piece of felt is hung on the door as a curtain. The interior is very warm in winter. Black tents are made of the wool of yaks, which does not seep water, so they will not leak even in the heavy rain. Black cotton candy rooms are square, with two wooden poles supporting a stick as a beam in the middle, and four pillars supporting it on all sides, and then more than a dozen wool ropes are used to tie it tightly. The dark sound of the tent is built with a long mud trough, which burns dry yak dung day and night. A long gap is opened in the middle of the top of the account as a chimney for the stove, and a piece of complex curtain is sewn on top, which can be covered when it snows and rains. Around the tent are piles of wooden boxes and leather bags, used as attached walls to prevent the invasion of wind and rain.

Their seats are divided by the stove, men on the left and women on the right, with few disturbances. If a newly arrived male guest mistakenly steps into the female host's seat on the right, it will easily cause their laughter. Their sleeping places at night are also the same, men on the left and women on the right. Even if they are husband and wife, they should be separated in this way on the surface. They mostly sleep in clothes, cross their waists as a quilt, and do not use lights at night. The firelight in the stove can illuminate the whole curtain. They get up and go to bed very early, and have a primitive way of life of getting up at sunrise and resting at sunset.

Mongolian Economy

The Mongolians in Jike Beach do not have a single tent that has a camel, because the pasture here is a prairie, which is not suitable for the survival of camels. It is said that the Panchen Lama had 200 camels placed here last year, and more than half of them had died in just a few months. The Qinghai Mongolians who raise camels are all in the "Salt Lake" and "Zidam" areas in Haixi, where there are deserts, so it is suitable for the survival of camels, the ships of the desert.

However, they raise a lot of cattle and sheep. A few wealthy families have thousands of sheep, hundreds of cattle, and hundreds of horses. Ordinary households that can support themselves also have one hundred sheep and dozens of cattle.

The nomadic people are also inevitably obligated to pay taxes to the local government. There are seventy tents in Jike Beach, and they share 1,000 yuan of grass tax every year. Half of them are poor and cannot afford the heavy tax, so only thirty to forty tents share it every year.

Local prices are: sheep three yuan, cattle twenty yuan, horse one hundred yuan, sheep wool ten yuan per dan, white lambskin one yuan per piece, black lambskin two yuan per piece, brick tea four yuan per package, wheat twenty yuan per dan of 500 jin, and qingke twelve yuan per dan of 900 jin.

Most people's economic conditions are very poor, and often their necessary daily necessities are dragged on by borrowing money. For example, a package of brick tea worth four yuan is raised to five yuan. By the next year, merchants will come to collect lambskins and sheep to ask for a price. As for their trading methods, they also mostly barter.

Although their economy is tight, the men are always happy and sit peacefully in the tent, not wanting to engage in production, so the interest on loans has reached 5%.

Jiangsong, City Patrol Chief Fraudulently Investigated 81

Huang Zuqiang, a patrol chief from the Second Substation in this city, led police officers to the fourth household of the twenty-fourth insurance of the fourth ward of Longtan Town around 10 pm on the 29th of last month. He falsely claimed that there was an official document from Taicang to arrest Cai Danren, who had just moved from Taicang. If he could produce 80 yuan for going abroad, the matter could be resolved. He also forced the Jia chief Li Jinfu to be invited over. In the end, he still returned the receipt. The matter was heard by the town chief of the town, who said that the patrol chief had repeatedly harassed the neighborhood in the name of investigating cigarettes. Now, he is extorting money and coercing the Jia chief. This not only harms the people but also damages the reputation of the police. He has sent a letter to the substation to report the matter. It is heard that Inspector Luo has verified that the matter is true. It is unknown how the authorities will punish him.

Suzhou, Fresh Meat Industry Asks for Exemption from Business Tax 82

The meat shops in Suzhou City have recently experienced a tight supply of pigs, and there may be no goods available for sale. Therefore, it is planned to stop slaughtering for several days starting on the 10th. The Fresh Meat Industry Association believes that this matter is related to the entire city market, so it specially convened a meeting of all members on the afternoon of the 9th to discuss solutions. The industry is also unable to bear the business tax levied by the Wuxian Business Tax Bureau, and it is necessary to reduce or exempt it. The industry already pays a tax of about 5 jiao per pig slaughtered. If they have to pay business tax again, they will be unable to bear it and it would violate the principle of one tax per item. A special request was submitted to the county chamber of commerce on the 9th, which was forwarded to the Ministry of Finance and the Jiangsu Provincial Government, requesting exemption from business tax. If business tax must be collected, please exempt the slaughter tax to comply with the government's one-tax-per-item law and maintain business.

All Sectors Maintain Commemoration of the May 9th National Humiliation 83

Yesterday was the May 9th National Humiliation Memorial Day. All entertainment venues in Suzhou were ordered by the county party headquarters to stop entertainment for one day to remember the humiliation. The county party headquarters held a memorial meeting at 10 am, attended by representatives from various agencies, organizations, and schools. Special Commissioner Sun Dan忱 chaired the meeting, reporting on the significance of the memorial. Representatives from various agencies then gave speeches. The meeting ended with slogans.

Dissolution of Three Trade Associations 84

The Wuxian Hardware, Sand Casting, and Stone Industry Associations were established one after another in 1932. Three years have passed, and the organizations are not sound and the work is at a standstill. The county party headquarters has repeatedly ordered rectification, but there is no solution, and there is no need for their existence. The Wuxian County Chamber of Commerce received instructions from the county party headquarters on the 9th, ordering the three trade associations to be dissolved.

Scandal at the Yarn Factory Comes to an End 85

Yan Xinqi, the factory manager of the Sulun Yarn Factory outside Panmen, and Pu Liangyuan, the director of factory affairs, had a mutual accusation case with Jiang Fengying, the leader of the female workers' warp group, and Zhu Yindi, a female worker, due to a love affair. The details have been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Zhu Yindi's case accusing Jiang Fengying of defamation and Jiang Fengying's case accusing Zhu Yindi of slander were both judged not guilty by the district court on the 7th. The district court also ruled on the afternoon of the 9th that it would not accept the two cases filed by Yan Xinqi and Pu Liangyuan against Zhu Yindi. The yarn factory scandal that was once a sensation has come to an end.

Wuxi: The Truth About the Explosion 86

It was previously reported in this newspaper that a loud explosion occurred at 2 PM on the 8th at Zhao Changsheng's residence, number 18, Yiyuan Alley, Chang'an Bridge, outside the North Gate. Wu Gonghe, an apprentice named Shen Hongxing from the Yiji Firecracker Shop, was killed instantly, and an elderly woman named Zhu Zhangshi and a child named Zhu Shengxian, along with five others, were injured. It is now known that the loud noise was indeed caused by an explosive detonation. Wu Gonghe and his apprentice Shen Hongxing, after lunch that day, were inside the Yiyuan Alley residence, mixing 15 catties of newly heated potassium nitrate with sulfur in a large earthenware basin, with a small jar of phosphorus nitrate placed on top. They intended to carry it in a bamboo basket to the shop in Tantou Alley to crush it and make firecrackers. However, when they reached the front of Zhao Changsheng's house, the phosphorus nitrate was heated by the vapor of the already heated potassium nitrate, causing the explosion. The entire city was shaken. At the time, the sound of gongs and drums was deafening, and people suspected a fire. Fire brigades from various districts rushed to the scene, only to discover that there was no fire, but rather an explosive detonation. The court was notified by the Fourth Precinct chief, and at 5 PM, Prosecutor Shen, accompanied by Coroner Wang, went to investigate. It was found that the deceased, Shen Hongxing, had his right eye blown away, and two holes were blown into his temple and next to his right ear. His pants were severely torn, with only a small piece of waist cloth remaining. His left leg was also blown off, and a large amount of flesh was blown away from the back of both legs, leaving a bloody mess. A piece of his cotton coat was blown off the back, and there were three burn wounds on the skin. It was confirmed that he died from injuries sustained in the explosion. Of the injured, Zhu Zhangshi had her right leg amputated. Chen Agou had his left eye blinded by the explosion. Zhu Shengbao had a hole blown into his forehead, and his large intestine was protruding from his abdomen. Shen Adong had a hole in his left shoulder, and a blood vessel was severed. His injuries were severe and life-threatening. Chen Jingeng sustained minor injuries and sought medical treatment on his own.

Zhenjiang: Nantong to be Developed as an Industrial Zone 87

The counties under the Yudi District of the Provincial Government, bordering the river and the sea, with convenient transportation and abundant produce, are most conducive to administrative and construction development. It is rumored that the Provincial Government plans to develop the Nantong District as an industrial zone. This project is currently under meticulous study and will be implemented as soon as the conference of the heads of ten provinces and departments concludes.

Jiangyin: Young Traveler in Hotel Attempts Suicide 88

At approximately 3 PM on the 6th (previous day), a traveler from Zhejiang checked into the Jiangyin Hotel on Jin Yi Street in the city. He immediately booked room number 30 upstairs. He registered in the guest book as Zhu Yu, from Zhenhai, Zhejiang, visiting friends in Jiangyin. That evening, he had dinner in the hotel and then sat down at his desk to write a suicide note. After writing about family matters, he swallowed more than twenty sleeping pills he had brought with him, as well as a pair of gold rings. He then turned off the light and went to bed. The next day, at approximately 2 PM, the tea server, Tang Hengcai, noticed that the traveler had not gotten up. Suspecting he had taken poison, he urgently reported it to the hotel owner, who in turn reported it to the Public Security Bureau. He also telegraphed Renji Hospital to administer an emergency injection. He was rushed to the hospital for treatment, and the poison was gradually expelled, allowing him to recover.

Nantong: Villager Riot 89

In Qinbei, Qinzhao, Oufang, and other villages near the mines, a misunderstanding arose recently during the conscription of young men. Villagers beat gongs and gathered a crowd of four to five thousand people, demanding the village chief remove names from the conscription list. When he refused, they ransacked the village office. Section Chief Wang Youwen of the County Government, Director Song Mingxin of the Public Security Bureau, and First District Chief Yan Yinan went to the villages to persuade them. The villagers even threatened to set fire and kill. The security team suppressed the riot and arrested seventeen ringleaders, including Xu Sunhuai and Suo, and took them to the County Government for interrogation. The disturbance is gradually calming down.

Haimen: Resolution of the Tonghai School Land Dispute 90

The long-standing dispute over the Kenmu School Land in Tonghai has now been resolved through negotiation and settlement. In addition to the Tongshi returning 90 shares to the county, Zhang Xiaoruo (agreed upon before his death) contributed 20 shares from his own production, and Zhang Jingli contributed 10 shares, totaling 120 shares to fund the county's primary schools. Furthermore, Tongshi will provide one free student from the county in each grade, for a total of three students. The Tong magician formula table Shen Yanmou and Yu Jingzhi are waiting in Shanghai. County representatives Director Yang Binru of the Education Bureau, Chen Zhenji, Hu Yongnian, and Shi Shuzhi will depart for Shanghai in August to sign the peace treaty and petition the Executive Yuan to withdraw the lawsuit.

Luhe: Elderly Woman Hangs Herself Out of Anger 91

In Binjiang Township, Fourth District of this county, there is a man named Zhou Zongshi who is fond of women. He recently committed adultery with the widow Wang Chuan, from Xinli Township, a neighboring village, and has been staying at her house, intending to become husband and wife. His aunt, Chuan's mother-in-law, was very angry at this situation and repeatedly warned her daughter-in-law, but Lin ignored her and even made excuses to avoid providing support. The pitiful Chuan, already seventy years old, seeing the shameful situation exposed, suddenly had the idea of leaving the world. Therefore, she hanged herself at night and died. It is truly tragic.

Ningbo: Wu Zhiyou Visits Xuebao 92

Central Supervisory Committee member Wu Zhiyun, accompanied by his friend Li Shuhua, arrived in Feng from Shanghai the day before yesterday (the 6th) to visit the scenic spot of Xuebao. At approximately 11 AM on the 7th, they paid respects at Jiang's mother's tomb in Yulin'ao. In the afternoon, they came to Ningbo from Feng and visited the Zhongshan Park in this port before returning to Shanghai by boat at 4 PM.

Shaoxing: Establishment of Pingcha Improvement Field in Najia Hall 93

Shaoxing Pingshui green tea is exported overseas in large quantities. The Zhejiang Construction Department, in order to improve tea leaves and increase production, recently decided to establish a tea improvement field. Yesterday, they sent staff to Shaoxing to investigate. As a result, they determined that Sanjie Town, at the border of Shaoxing, Sheng County, and Xinchang County, has convenient transportation and an excellent environment. They decided to acquire or long-term lease several hundred acres of land from the people to establish the site and use the existing buildings to reorganize and construct a factory to meet the needs. The Executive Committee has approved an allocation of 14,000 yuan for preliminary expenses.

Local News

Representatives from All Sectors of This City Hold a National Humiliation Memorial Meeting Yesterday; Chairman Wang Manyun Reports on the Significance of the Commemoration; The Entire City Flies Flags at Half-Mast and Stops Entertainment to Mourn 94

Yesterday (the 9th) was National Humiliation Memorial Day. In addition to Yuan Shikai's traitorous act of signing the Twenty-One Demands proposed by Japan to seek imperial power, disregarding the humiliation, other events such as the "August 29th" Opium War defeat and the signing of the Treaty of Nanjing, which marked the beginning of unequal treaties, as well as "May 3rd," "May 30th," "June 23rd," and "September 7th," are all national humiliations that must never be forgotten. The Municipal Party Headquarters specially convened representatives from all sectors yesterday morning at 10 AM to hold a memorial meeting. The meeting place was the headquarters' auditorium, which was decorated quite solemnly. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Attending Representatives

Party Committee Member Wang Manyun and all staff members of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Zai Zongjian of the Jianghai Customs Superintendency, Tan Gengxin of the Audit Office, Lin Kecong of the Municipal Women's Association, Huang Zaoxiong of the Municipal Education Association, Zhou Xuexiang of the General Labor Union, Xiao Huiqing of the Municipal Farmers' Association, Shi Miaoxing of the Buddhist Association, Mao Yun of the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association, Zhu Yangwu of the First Special District Citizens' Association, Huang Xianggu of the Second Special District Citizens' Association, Wang Longzhang of the People's Association and Common Knowledge Association, Du Mengsen of the Cooperative Enterprise Promotion Association, Wang Xuequan of the Chinese Education Federation, Zhu Shide of the National Goods Maintenance Association, and more than 500 representatives from various agencies, fellow-provincial associations, trade associations, labor unions, major universities and schools, district party headquarters, and district branches.

Meeting Order

All stand at attention; sing the Party song; bow three times to the Party and national flag and the portrait of the Founding Father; the Chairman respectfully reads the Founding Father's will; three minutes of silence; the Chairman reports; speeches; shouting slogans; adjournment.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Wang Manyun, Recorder Du Mengsen, Master of Ceremonies Zhang Hanyun. After the rituals, the Chairman gave a report, stating in brief: "Today is a day of commemorating national humiliation. If we want to save the nation and strive for survival, we can only bury our heads and work hard. Besides preparing ourselves for sacrifice and struggle, there is no other way out. Therefore, we must recognize the following points: 1. Strengthen national defense so that imperialists have no opportunity to invade. 2. Strive for production and construction to resist foreign economic aggression. 3. Implement the New Life Movement and promote labor service to restore national consciousness and inherent morality. Finally, I hope that everyone will fulfill their duty to prepare and work together." Then slogans were shouted, and the meeting was adjourned.

Slogans

Unite everyone, strive to strengthen national defense, strive for production and construction, implement the New Life Movement vigorously, promote the national labor service movement, eliminate all traitors, long live the Chinese Kuomintang, long live the Republic of China, long live the liberation of the Chinese nation!

Half-Mast Alert

Yesterday was National Humiliation Memorial Day. In addition to sending representatives to participate in the memorial meeting convened by the Municipal Party Headquarters, all agencies, organizations, schools, and party headquarters at all levels in this city held separate memorial ceremonies and flew flags at half-mast in mourning. The Municipal Public Security Bureau, Security General Corps, and the Public Concession and French Concession Police Departments implemented alerts to prevent petty disturbances.

Entertainment Suspended

Yesterday, in addition to convening the memorial meeting and flying flags at half-mast, all entertainment was suspended in this city because it was the most tragic and grievous day for China. All entertainment venues, movie theaters, and opera houses such as Little World, Fu'an, Penglai, Republic, World, Shanghai, Guangdong, and Fuxing were closed for one day to commemorate the national humiliation.

Machinery Industry Association Cables the Government to Suppress Smuggling in North China 95

The United Association of Mechanical National Goods Factories in this city, due to rampant smuggling in North China, which has recently been transported south by rail, has been severely affected, and sales have been sluggish. Therefore, it held an ad hoc executive committee meeting at Tongxinglou at 8 PM the day before yesterday. More than 20 representatives from the Wuzhou Pharmacy, the Family Industrial Society, the Yapu'er Electrical Appliance Factory, and the China Chemical Industry Society, among others, attended, with Secretary-General Cheng Shouchong present. After discussion, regarding the proposal of "How to deal with smuggling in North China affecting domestic industry and commerce," it was resolved to telegraph the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Industry, and the Ministry of Finance to strictly suppress it to maintain industry. Regarding the proposal of "It is rumored that the central government intends to reduce import duties on sugar and rayon, how should it be handled?" it was resolved to handle it in conjunction with the smuggling case. It was resolved to have Dong Xixiang draft the telegram. Passed.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Persuades Ice-Fresh Industry Yesterday to Join the Fish Market; Representatives of the Industry Promise to Consider and Reply to the Fish Market Board of Directors Tomorrow; The Fish Market Board of Directors Reviewed the Qualifications of Brokers Yesterday 96

The Shanghai Fish Market will hold an opening ceremony tomorrow morning at 10 AM. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, acting on the instructions of the Ministry of Industry, invited representatives of the ice-fresh fish industry for talks yesterday afternoon, earnestly urging them to join the market. The Board of Directors held a meeting at 4 PM yesterday afternoon to prepare for the opening. The details are recorded below.

The Chamber of Commerce Obeys Orders to Persuade Them to Join

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce invited members of the ice-fresh industry association, including Gongda, Qianfeng, and Shengji, a total of 13 companies, for talks at 2 PM yesterday afternoon. A total of six representatives attended, and Chairman Yu Zuoting and Secretary Yan E'sheng advised them. First, they reported that they were obeying the Ministry of Industry's order to deeply understand the central government's intention to improve fish market transactions, urging them to join the fish market and earnestly comply. Then, the representatives stated that there were practical difficulties in joining the fish market, roughly divided into three points: 1. It is not easy to recover the loans previously extended by the fish shops. 2. It is impossible to maintain business with a commission of 3.5%. 3. The market is too far away, and transportation is inconvenient. They asked to consider the difficulties of the merchants and said that if the government had relief measures, the fish merchants would all agree. After Chairman Yu's repeated persuasion, the representatives agreed to go back and consider and reply on Monday. The meeting adjourned at approximately 3 PM.

The Market's Board of Directors Held a Meeting Yesterday

The Fish Market Board of Directors held a meeting at the Zhonghui Bank on Edward Road at 4 PM yesterday afternoon. Chairman Du Yuesheng, Standing Directors Fang Jiaobo, Tang Chengzong, and Kui Yanfang, Directors Qu Hewu, Zhang Fayao, Lin Kanghou, Yu Qiaqing, Yu Kaizhan, and Zhang Shenzhi attended. General Manager Wang Xiaolai, Deputy General Manager Zhu Kaiguan, and Sun Guchen were also present. After Chairman Du Yuesheng's report, they discussed all matters concerning the opening ceremony at 10 AM on the 11th and the start of business at 3 AM on the 12th. Regarding the 40 brokers, it was resolved to hand them over to the Standing Committee, together with the General and Deputy General Managers, for review. The meeting adjourned at approximately 6 PM.

The Market Announces Opening Declaration

The Fish Market issued a declaration yesterday, saying, "Today, when statisticians discuss China, they use figures of over 400 million people and over 3.4 million square miles of Chinese territory, and over 270,000 square miles of Chinese territorial waters. They also know that the land is rich in resources but has not been fully developed, the ocean's production has not been fully utilized, and the people's strength has not been fully exhausted. Weighing the content of its strength, it is determined to be the strongest. Compared with the world's powers, everyone knows that no one can surpass it. This is why people ridicule us as a sleeping lion, and why Mussolini sighs that Italy does not have land as vast as China. Therefore, China's weakness, and even the painful experience of invasion, is not due to a lack of innate endowments, but rather to the failure of human affairs. This is why the ruling officials encourage the people to rely on their own efforts. To rely on one's own efforts means to estimate one's own strength, make good use of one's own strength, and develop one's own strength. Chairman Chiang's promotion of the New Life Movement, the initiative of national economic construction, and Minister Kong's plan for production and construction all deeply understand that the development of people's power and the acquisition and use of production are not fully exhausted. To follow the meaning of self-reliance, cultivate people's power, and advance production in order to seek the soundness of the national economic organization, it is a strategy of the ancient sages who valued the people's livelihood and enriched the country. The Ministry of Industry's establishment of the Shanghai Fish Market, initiated by former Minister Chen and completed by Minister Wu now, is aimed at following the Founding Father's legacy of government and people cooperation, reorganizing the fishing industry, and implementing the policy of saving the country through production that is needed today. China's fishing villages are scattered among the seven coastal provinces, and the total number of fishermen and fish merchants reaches tens of millions, comparable to the entire population of Britain and Germany. It is conceivable that the relationship with national power is of great importance. Therefore, our people should do their best to cooperate with the government's well-intentioned policies to reorganize the fishing industry and help it succeed, not only the fishermen and fish merchants should work together harmoniously. When reforming a business, at the beginning of the reform, there are often concerns, and some mistakenly believe that the reorganization agency will have facilities that are unfavorable to the past. This is actually confined to a corner of perspective, not a study of the overall situation, only counting the interests of a few people, not the interests of the country. According to a survey in 1933, the value of the nation's fishery products was approximately 50 million yuan, the value of imported foreign fish was approximately 40 million yuan, and it is estimated that the value of the territorial waters' fishery production in one year is approximately 400 million yuan. It can be seen that there is still surplus production, consumption has been encroached upon, and the path for fishery development is great and broad. Furthermore, in recent years, the decline of the fishing industry has been caused by economic weakness, the rampant acts of pirates, the dumping of foreign fish, or the mistake of useless competition. It is not caused by overproduction or insufficient consumption. Therefore, the necessity of reorganizing fishery administration is very obvious and there is no doubt that it is urgently needed in practice. Now, the government, based on the bright idea of developing the economy and saving the country through production, entrusts the responsibility of reorganizing fishery administration and guiding fishermen to this market. This is the mission of this market, which should plan to remove obstacles to the fishing industry and further seek ways to protect the fishing industry in order to make the goal of building a national economy, can speed up the completion of the period due to the development of fish production. Therefore, not only should the colleagues of this market comply with this will, work hard, and the fishermen of each fishing village should admire the good governance, work hard, and the fish merchants who are engaged in the fishing industry should carefully examine the advantages and disadvantages, eliminate jealousy and concerns, and seek sincere cooperation. Otherwise, our country's fishing industry will not only be insufficient to talk about construction, but also may not be able to survive in the international community where control is prevalent. This greatly affects economic construction. Out of love for ourselves and love for the country, we sincerely declare and hope that the wise will correct us."

Asahadi and Yu Zuoting Discuss Sino-Philippine Trade 97

After arriving in Shanghai, Philippine Congressman and Chairman of the Foreign Affairs Committee Asahadi has been repeatedly welcomed by all sectors. Then, Chairman Yu Zuoting of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce replied that the shortcoming of Philippine trade with China lies in the lack of publicity. Other countries have brokers selling grain in South China, and their prices are very low. However, China and the Philippines are like brothers. If they can connect with each other and establish a financial institution so that merchants of the two countries can use it to regulate finances and open up Sino-Philippine routes so that goods can be transported directly, it will definitely benefit the trade between the two countries greatly. Finally, Asahadi thanked Chairman Yu for his hospitality, shook hands, and departed.

Silk Cocoons Loan Syndicate; Loan Application Procedures; Open for Applications on Sunday as Usual 99

The Jiangsu-Zhejiang Spring Cocoon Collection Loan Syndicate for the 25th year, after starting to accept applications on the 6th of this month, has seen a steady stream of cocoon merchants going to register in recent days. In order to facilitate the manufacturers, the syndicate will be open for business as usual on Sundays. The following is an exploration of the syndicate's loan methods: 1. Total Loan Amount: This syndicate is organized and managed by the silver and money industry to benefit cocoon farmers and assist the silk industry with all matters related to the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces' spring cocoon collection for the 25th year. The total loan amount is provisionally set at 30 million national currency. 2. Loan Application: All manufacturers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces may negotiate with the syndicate for loans, specifically for the purpose of collecting cocoons, but they should submit the following items, filled out on the application form, to the syndicate's general office or branch office before the published application deadline. After review, they will be registered. 1. Manufacturer's name, address, amount of equipment capital, names and addresses of managers and shareholders. 2. Loan amount. 3. Estimated quantity of dried cocoons to be collected, name and address of cocoon company, number of kilns. 4. Name, occupation, and address of guarantor. 5. Loan interest rate: 8.5 percent per month. 6. Loan term: Up to three months. 7. Loan Deposit: When the borrower signs the loan contract with the syndicate, they should prepay the syndicate a deposit of at least 30%. During the loan period, if the syndicate believes that the deposit paid by the borrower is insufficient for the agreed percentage, the borrower shall immediately replenish the full amount after being notified by the syndicate. 8. Supervision and Management: From the time the manufacturer collects the cocoons until the dried cocoons are loaded onto the stack, the syndicate will send personnel to supervise and manage. The cost (a fee of 20 cents per picul of dried cocoons) will be borne by the borrower. However, the borrower will still provide lodging for the supervisors. The scope of supervision is as follows: 1. When using the loan to start weighing, the borrower shall withdraw it in batches from the bank designated by the syndicate. 2. Cocoon Collection: The borrower shall collect cocoons according to the published cocoon price and submit a daily cocoon collection report to the syndicate's supervisor for review. 3. Transportation of Dried Cocoons: After the cocoons are baked and packaged, the syndicate's supervisor will weigh them together and transport them to the warehouse designated by the syndicate. 4. Insurance: The insurance of cocoons and pledges will be handled separately by the syndicate, and the insurance premiums will be borne by the borrower. 5. The right to dispose of the pledges will be handled in accordance with the regulations of the cocoon loan note.

The Spring Silkworm Cocoons of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces Are About to Enter the Market: Manufacturers Borrow Funds to Purchase Cocoons; the Lending Syndicate Will Soon Examine and Approve Loan Amounts; Estimated Output of One Million Bales; Silk Factories Prepare to Commence Production 100

The spring silkworm cocoons of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are about to enter the market, with a total estimated output of about one million bales. Banks and native banks are organizing a syndicate to handle cocoon purchases and loans. Thirty-six silk factories in Shanghai are preparing to start their machinery. Details are as follows:

Syndicate Examines Loan Applications

A total of twenty banks and native banks, including the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, have jointly formed the 25th-year spring cocoon purchase lending syndicate. The total amount for handling cocoon purchases and loans is 30 million yuan, with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications each committing 5 million yuan, and eighteen banks, including the Shanghai Bank, jointly committing 20 million yuan. Subsequently, the China Remittance Bank and the Zhengming Bank joined, with their share coming from the amounts already committed by the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. The deadline for applications has been set for today, and no further applications will be accepted. Silk manufacturers from Shanghai, Hangzhou, Wuxi, and other places have been eagerly applying for loans, and the syndicate's standing committee is reviewing and approving them on an ongoing basis. The deadline for Zhejiang is the 20th, and for Jiangsu, the 25th. No extensions will be granted. Although today is a Sunday, when banks are normally closed, the syndicate will still be operating as usual.

Cocoon Output Estimated at One Million Bales

According to the distribution of silkworm eggs in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, this year's spring cocoon output, based on a good harvest, is estimated at a total of about one million bales (market weight). Improved varieties account for 70%, and local varieties account for 30%. New cocoons from Haining, Shaoxing, and other places in Zhejiang are expected to enter the market around the 18th, and new cocoons from Wuxi, Liyang, and other places in Jiangsu are expected to enter the market around the 25th. Silk manufacturers and cocoon merchants from various places are forming cocoon purchasing organizations, borrowing funds from banks and native banks, and preparing to depart for various places to purchase cocoons. At the same time, public security bureaus and river police units in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have dispatched police to provide strict protection for merchants purchasing cocoons.

Shanghai Factories Prepare to Commence Production

Silk manufacturers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have decided to commence silk reeling immediately after the new cocoons enter the market. In Shanghai, a total of thirty-six factories have reported to the Silk Manufacturers' Association that they will purchase spring cocoons and commence silk reeling this year. They are currently repairing their factory buildings and machinery in preparation for commencing production. In the spring of the 19th year of the Republic, there were a total of 113 single and double palace silk factories in Shanghai. However, due to a sharp drop in silk prices, almost all of them ceased operations. Although the number of factories commencing operations this year has increased to thirty-six, it is only about one-third of the peak number.
