Moving Fast Horse 207

— Ziding

This is a very fun toy that you can make and play with using a piece of cardboard.

First, you draw the simple drawing A below—a person riding a horse on paper. You see that although the horse in the picture only has two legs and the rider only has one arm, the moving horse legs and human arm need to be added. You color picture A, stick it on the cardboard, and cut it out. Second, draw the added two horse legs and a whip-holding human arm as shown in Figure B, color them, stick them on the cardboard, and cut them out.

Third, put the cut-out picture A upside down on the table, and place the added horse legs in a proper position to create a running posture. At the same time, put the rider's arm holding the whip in place. To do this, you need a pushing rod. This rod is very important. You must use it to make the horse and man move. What is the material for making this rod? You can use a strip of cardboard, but it is best to use "a thin piece of wood, which is more durable. After drilling holes in the aligned horse legs and human arm and connecting them with a thread, drill two small holes above the tightly joined horse legs, place the rod horizontally, align it with the two small holes, drill two small holes in the rod, and connect them with a thread. Finally, make a gap in the center of the rod to accommodate the whip. The toy can be considered successful at this point, as shown in Figure C.

Turning Figure C over is Figure D. When playing, you only need to push the rod on the toy back and forth to see the horse running very fast, and the rider's arm is also moving very lively, just like a real person. Children, this toy is very good. In your spare time, you can try making it.

What Do Lions, Tigers, and Elephants Eat in the Circus? 208

— Lu Guowei

Yesterday, Miner went to see the circus with his father. After the show, Miner asked his father, "Dad, what do the tigers, lions, elephants, etc. that do circus tricks eat every day?" After listening to Miner's question, his father thought for a while and replied, "I don't understand very well myself. Let's go ask." They went to a circus staff member and politely asked, "Sir, would you be willing to tell us what these wild animals eat?" The staff member listened and replied politely, "I am very willing, very willing. If you don't mind the tediousness, let me slowly tell you. A normal middle-aged lion needs to eat 30 to 40 catties of beef every day, and tigers are about the same. Elephants are gluttonous. They eat 55 catties of buckwheat, chaff, sweet potatoes, radishes, bananas, etc. a day. And elephants also like to drink very much. They can drink forty or fifty bottles of beer without getting drunk. When the weather is cold, each elephant drinks a bottle of whiskey (a very strong wine) to keep warm. Do you think that's amazing? There are also monkeys of all sizes, who also have to eat a meal and two teas every day. A lot of milk and sugar are added to the tea, and the meal is made of fruits and vegetables. On average, we spend a total of three hundred yuan every day to provide their food."

After listening to the staff member's words, Miner's father and Miner thanked him respectfully and went home happily.

Whales and Fish 209

— Little Shrimp

A whale is a mammal with a huge body, six or seven zhang long. Because it lives in the water, everyone calls it "whale fish." Because it is called "whale fish," some people think that it must also be a fish, just like ordinary fish. But it's not. A whale is a whale and a fish is a fish.

The body of a whale is ten million times larger than that of a fish; the body of a fish is covered with scales, while the body of a whale has nothing; the blood of a whale is warm, while the blood of a fish is cold; a whale is born alive, while a fish is born from eggs; a whale breathes with lungs, and a fish breathes with gills. The most obvious thing besides the whale's extremely large body is their two tails. When drawing whales, most people draw their tails like fish, which is a big mistake.

Why? The tail shape of a whale is flat and round, while the tail shape of a fish is flat and straight (see the top circle). However, most people often have wrong ideas, so such jokes are made! Here, I attach two tail diagrams to correct the mistakes that children have made before.

What Kind of Person Will I Be in the Future 210

— Jiang Zhen, Grade 4, No. 1 Elementary School in Hankou City

(14th Place)

Our country is now very weak and oppressed by powerful enemies, and cannot be revived. We are all young children and should not shout empty slogans of saving the country. Everyone should have a firm ambition: "What kind of person will I be in the future to save the country?"

What is my ambition? It is to be a doctor with scientific research! Now I write the reason for my ambition below:

First, because doctors in our country now generally do not have scientific research methods to improve; what's more, some have no knowledge at all, read a few medical books, and come to be doctors, diagnosing and treating inexplicably. Therefore, many people have suffered from them; weren't my aunt and grandfather both killed by taking the wrong medicine? Therefore, I must use scientific research methods to improve Chinese medicine in the future!

Second, because being a doctor is beneficial to the country. In addition to being able to diagnose and treat patients and save the lives of many compatriots, if we start a war with the enemy, we doctors can also go to the front line to rescue the wounded soldiers who are fighting for the country. Isn't this of great help to the country?

Third, because doctors now only know how to make money and do not help the poor at all! So that many poor compatriots cannot be cured and die! This is really too bad! Therefore, I will definitely help the poor and be a life-saving doctor in the future.

For these three reasons: to improve Chinese medicine, to rescue front-line soldiers, and to help the poor, my ambition is determined to be a doctor with scientific research! Save the Chinese nation—and save all mankind!

Continuous Story Painting (Part 2) 211

— Zhang Youjian

Still Belongs to Me

Rong'er was catching shrimp with a small net and heard footsteps behind him. He quickly turned his head to look, and a bamboo box full of mulberries and snacks suddenly disappeared!

Fei Jian opened the box and saw it was full of things. He was extremely happy and wanted to move it to the ground to eat it all by himself.

Rong'er realized that his box had been stolen by Fei'er, so he quietly put the small net on the ground next to Fei'er. Fei'er moved everything out of the box and placed it on the ground. He didn't know that they had all been placed into Rong'er's small net.

Rong'er knew that everything in the box was in the small net, and immediately carried it on his shoulders and left: "Ha! Ha! So many things still belong to me!"

The Tale of a Loyal Dog (18) 212

— Xinqing

This kind of work was very hard for Bosui Xi. Over these several years, Xiao Nanluo gradually became a strong young man, while it aged year by year. Its legs had become stiff, and its bones often ached, yet it still refused to slacken in the work it should do. Xiao Nanluo very much wanted it to save some energy and pull the cart himself, but how could Bode Xi agree? The only help it could accept was a push from Xiao Nanluo from behind whenever it got stuck in icy ruts. But Bode Xi was used to the work of pulling the cart all its life, and it felt very proud of itself. Although it endured the torment of ice and frost, the bumps of the road, and the soreness of its muscles and bones, it held its breath, lowered its head, and continued forward relentlessly.

Nanluo had repeatedly said to his beloved dog, "Bode Xi, take a rest at home. At your age, it's time to rest. I can pull the cart myself." But even though Bode Xi understood his good intentions, it never wanted to stay put. Putting its body between the two cart shafts and walking step by step in the snow, its footprints had been constantly imprinted there for the past several years.

Bode Xi thought to itself, "No one should rest unless they are dead." Yet it also felt that the time for it to rest seemed not far off. Its eyesight was no longer as clear as before, and it felt pain in its back when it got up after a night's sleep. However, every time it heard the bells of the temple strike five, it knew that day had broken and work should begin, and it would never lie in the straw pile again.

The old gentleman often reached out his withered hand to stroke Bode Xi's head, saying, "Poor Bode Xi, you and I will soon be quietly lying together." At that time, the old man's heart and the old dog's heart held the same thought and the same sorrow, wondering who would take care of their beloved Xiao Nanluo after they both passed away.

One afternoon, they returned from Ang'er through the snow. The plains were covered in thick snow, which had frozen solid and smooth, like marble. As they walked along, they suddenly found a beautiful little wooden doll lying on the road, playing a small drum. It was six inches tall, wearing red and vermilion clothes, and when they picked it up, it was not damaged at all. It was indeed a very beautiful toy. Xiao Nanluo wanted to find its owner, but he couldn't find them. He secretly thought that this thing would be very suitable to give to Xiao Ai Luo, who would definitely be happy to see it.

It was already night when he passed the mill. He knew that was where Xiao Ai Luo's room was, with its small window. He thought that since the two of them often played together, there would be no harm in giving her this little thing.

Below her room, there was a small shed. He climbed onto the sloping shed roof and gently knocked on the windowpane a few times, only to see that there was a light on inside. Xiao Ai Luo opened the window and looked out, showing some surprise.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Philosophy Lecture

Critique of Kant's Agnosticism 214

— Jing Yin

Immanuel Kant is one of the great thinkers of modern times. His philosophical thought, in a certain sense, is unique, just like Hegel and Feuerbach. If viewed formally, his views can be said to be not entirely the same as extreme idealism and general materialism. On the one hand, he acknowledges that things exist objectively, but on the other hand, he stands on the ground of a priori idealism. He once said: "We have no knowledge prior to experience; all our knowledge begins with experience." The so-called experience here, of course, refers to our experience of objectively existing things. Since Kant believed that knowledge comes from experience and is not innate, he naturally acknowledges the objective existence of things. At the same time, he also believes that the analysis of knowledge starts from the problem of sensation. In his view, sensation is the result of objectively existing things touching our minds and giving them influence. In other words, it means that sensation is caused by the contact between our senses, brain, and objectively existing things. This view not only shows that things exist objectively but also shows that human sensations, ideas, and thoughts are caused by objective things stimulating their senses and brains, and do not exist independently of objective things. From this point of view alone, Kant can be said to be a materialist. However, on the other hand, Kant is also clinging to a priori idealism. After expressing the above views, he went on to say: "Although all our knowledge begins with experience, not all our knowledge originates from experience. For it is very possible that our experience itself is composed of two kinds of elements: one is obtained from the impression of the senses, and the other is the mental part that our cognitive function innately adds to the impression of external things when it receives the impression of external objects. Therefore, this is not an easy question, and it cannot be answered lightly. It must be carefully considered before some certainty can be grasped. Is there any knowledge that not only breaks away from experience, but also breaks away from all impressions of the senses and exists independently? This kind of knowledge can be called a priori knowledge to distinguish it from empirical knowledge – a kind of knowledge that originates from a posteriori or experience." In this way, he immediately fell into the quagmire of idealism.

In such a contradiction, in retreating from materialism to idealism, Kant became a famous agnostic. He stated that we cannot but admit that things exist, but what exactly are things like? What exactly are things? This is something we absolutely cannot know. Things exist, but we cannot fully know the nature of things, things themselves. What we can know is not things themselves, but the phenomena that appear to us, things within the limits that we can see. Such agnosticism is the center of Kant's philosophy.

Kant himself said that his philosophy is idealism in the a priori and realism in the empirical. Therefore, on the question of the occurrence and constitution of thought and knowledge, he stands on the ground of realism, that is, he admits the objective existence of things; but on the question of how universally valid knowledge is, he stands on the ground of idealism, believing that the nature of things themselves is unknowable.

However, the position of realism and the position of idealism are incompatible. If things exist objectively apart from our minds, and if human ideas are a reflection of objectively existing things, then there can be no knowledge that transcends experience and the senses; conversely, if thought and knowledge are a priori and things are subordinate to the mind, then there can be no objectively existing things. Naturally, human sensations, thoughts, and consciousness are not only passive, but also have a positive and active reaction to objective things, because human senses are dynamic, not dead static objects. When receiving objective things, they can also play an active role; but this subjective active role of human beings is by no means independent and a priori, but occurs under the condition of objectively existing things. Therefore, the relationship between things and mind, objective and subjective, reality and idea, is not parallel. Kant juxtaposed the two, and the result was that he became a mysterious agnostic; in the final analysis, he was still an idealist. Strictly speaking, in philosophical thought, there is only the opposition between materialism and idealism; there can be no middle ground compromise outside this opposition. Kant's philosophy, in its achievements and in the appearance of its system, can be said to be unique, but in the final analysis, he is still a mysterious idealist; the only difference between him and general idealists lies only in the form of expression, or even only in the terms used.

Furthermore, since things exist objectively, and since humans can reflect objective things into thoughts and knowledge within a certain time and space, why can't we use this knowledge to understand those objective things? According to Kant, we can only know the phenomena that things present, not their noumenon, so things themselves are unknowable. However, the so-called phenomenon of things is the expression of its noumenon; the phenomenon is not something else that is opposed to the noumenon. If human senses and knowledge have an active role, then why can't people synthesize and penetrate the phenomena expressed by things to understand and know their noumenon? Naturally, human knowledge is subject to the limitations of time and space and can only be recognized and know the fixed noumenon of things within a certain time and space. It cannot transcend time and space to recognize things that are not yet knowable, but within a certain time and space, we can indeed recognize its noumenon through the phenomena that things show at that time. Kant's agnosticism believes that there is no possibility of recognizing and knowing things at all, which is another expression of mysterious idealism.

Engels and Ulyanov had a very correct criticism of Kant. According to them, the thing-in-itself, as Kant said, cannot be absolutely separated from the phenomenon. The thing-in-itself is expressed as a phenomenon, "the thing-in-itself is the thing for us." Agnosticism about the thing-in-itself is nothing more than one of the erroneous conclusions of the metaphysical theory of mechanically separating the thing-in-itself from the phenomenon—this is a very correct judgment.

World Knowledge

Current Status of Major News Agencies in the World 215

— Xiyun

News agencies can be said to be the assisting organs of newspapers and magazines. Their task is to establish communication networks in various parts of the world, collect various news items, and transmit them to newspapers, magazines, and other organizations by extremely rapid means. Because they have such a task, their propaganda effect is very great, and countries around the world pay great attention to the news agency business. When the situation is tense, the news agency activities of various countries are particularly important and can play an active role. Not to mention the distant past, just the activities and roles of major news agencies in the world in the recent Italian-Abyssinian War can give us a general idea. According to investigations, at the beginning of the war, there were as many as eighty or ninety special correspondents from news agencies around the world in Addis Ababa, and now there are more than a hundred. These correspondents work almost every minute. They constantly transmit news of the war, especially news that is beneficial to their own countries, to London, Rome, Paris, Berlin, New York, Tokyo, and other places, so that the military actions of Italy and Abyssinia can be reflected in the eyes of people all over the world within a few hours. Among them, the activities of the British Reuters news agency were particularly active and effective. Its correspondents in Addis Ababa constantly propagated to the world the atrocities of the Italian army, the heroic resistance of the Abyssinian people, and all news that was beneficial to Britain. Although the Italian Stefani news agency tried hard to compete with it, the result was that Reuters' news spread all over the world. From the beginning of the Italian-Abyssinian War until now, the main reason why world opinion hates and condemns Italy is of course that people generally have a sense of justice to sympathize with small and weak nations and oppose the aggressive actions of imperialism, but the news propaganda of Reuters also plays an indispensable role in this.

Speaking of the organization of international news agencies, almost every country has one. The countries participating in the "National News Agency Alliance" mainly include 28 countries such as Britain, the United States, France, and Germany, and there are also 28 major news agencies among them. Here we can only list a few of the most famous major news agencies in the world to give a general description.

British Reuters News Agency

This was originally founded by Julius Reuter, a German in the mid-19th century. Later, because this German transferred his nationality to Britain, the Reuters news agency he founded became the property of the British. At first, Reuters only used carrier pigeons to conduct commercial communications; it was not until it moved to London in 1851 that it used telegraph to transmit news, establishing its position in the news communication industry; then, with the overseas development of Britain, it established communication networks all over the world and became the center of the "World News Agency Alliance." The news agencies of various countries almost have to rely on it as a medium to connect.

Reuters is a special agency for transmitting foreign communications, which is different from the representative news agencies of other countries in this regard. Britain has another news agency that specializes in transmitting domestic news, called The Press Association. It has a close organic relationship with Reuters, and the two help each other to complete the task of domestic and foreign communications. Currently, The Press Association

Page 22

has more than 130 branches throughout Britain, using 3,000 miles of privately installed wires to transmit domestic news and distribute Reuters' foreign news to the country. Reuters relies mainly on this British domestic communication agency to collect British news for foreign news agencies that have an agreement with it.

The relationship between Reuters and the British domestic communication agency was initially only a simple mutual cooperation, but later this communication agency became increasingly powerful, forcing Reuters to have a closer relationship with it; in 1925, Reuters even offered more than half of its profits to it, effectively transferring control to it. By now, although the name of Reuters still exists independently, it has actually been merged into The Press Association.

United Press Association of America

Commonly abbreviated as AP, Chinese newspapers often write it as "Meilianshe." It is jointly composed of 1,285 newspapers in the United States and is a purely news-collecting and disseminating agency. It is not for profit. The funds it needs are shared by the news agencies participating in this communication agency. The principle is not to raise capital and not to seek profits. As for the executive agency of the news agency, it is a council mutually elected by the participating news agencies.

The Associated Press can be said to be a cooperative business jointly run by 1,285 newspapers in the United States. On the one hand, these newspapers have the obligation to provide news to the communication agency regularly and without compensation, and on the other hand, the communication agency often distributes all the news it collects to these newspapers. They have a spider web-like dedicated wire network of 225,000 miles. This communication agency sends out an average of 100,000 words of news every day.

Although this communication agency is jointly run by many newspapers in the United States, and although two or three thousand newspapers regularly provide its news without compensation, its annual expenses are also more than nine million US dollars; its scale is the largest in the world. At the same time, it is also unique among the world's news agencies in that it is jointly run by many newspapers.

French Havas News Agency

This can be said to be the largest and only news agency in France. In addition to transmitting news, it also operates advertising agency business. Historically, the establishment of Havas was actually earlier than Reuters. Now, in addition to gaining a monopolistic position in France, it also shows great strength in Spain, Portugal, and South America.

Havas is also one of the centers of the "World News Agency Alliance." Due to its development, Reuters' position has also been weakened. In the current world news agencies, Havas is as valued as Reuters.

German Wolff Telegraph News Agency

Before the Great War, Eastern Europe, Northern Europe, and Central Europe can be said to have been all the territories of Wolff, but after the war, with the decline of German power, it also lost its original territory. Now, it is still the largest communication agency in Germany. As for the organization, Wolff, like Havas, is a joint-stock company.

Italian Stefani News Agency

This was originally a news agency formed by joining the French Havas.

organization, but it has now become the only international communication agency officially run by Italy. Its current task is to promote the aggressive doctrines of the Blackshirt Prime Minister. After the outbreak of the Italian-Abyssinian War, it kept propagandizing the victory of the "civilized" army, but in fact, apart from newspapers under Mussolini's control publishing its news, it seems that no one accepted its communications. This is partly because most people do not sympathize with the use of poison gas to poison small and weak nations, and partly because the organization of this news agency is small and its power is weak.

Soviet TASS News Agency

TASS is the abbreviation of the Telegraph Agency of the Soviet Union. Originally, the Soviet Union's foreign communication agency after the October Revolution was initially the Rota News Agency, but in 1926 it withdrew from the international communication system, and the TASS news agency replaced it.

Although TASS also participates in the "World News Agency Alliance," it is essentially different from Reuters and Havas. If Reuters and Havas are the political megaphones of British and French imperialism, then TASS is a powerful news propaganda weapon of the Soviet Union. It not only transmits general news, but also pays special attention to news about various contradictions in the current world, and constantly disseminates to the world the true situation of news that Reuters and others are unwilling to transmit or distort.

Like Reuters has a close relationship with the British domestic communication agency and newspapers, TASS also has a deep relationship with the domestic communication agencies of the Soviet Union. They help each other in the collection and dissemination of news. However, the news agencies in the Soviet Union are state-owned. Although TASS is mutually dependent on domestic communication agencies, it is also constrained by domestic communication agencies. In this respect, it can be said that the situation is also different from that of Reuters.

Japan News Federation Originally, Japan's international communication was occupied by Reuters. However, since the establishment of this News Federation in 1924, Reuters has also lost this area. This News Federation is jointly formed by the eight major newspapers in Tokyo, Osaka, and other places; its organizational principle is similar to that of the United Press Association of America.

In Japan, there is also the Telegraph Communication Agency, which is opposed to this News Federation. However, although these two are the largest communication agencies in Japan, their transmission of international news still depends on European and American communication agencies.

Recently, in order to strengthen news propaganda, Japan has seen the merger of the Union and Dentsu. At the same time, in strengthening news control, Japan has recently seen the establishment of the Allied News Agency with the Union as its parent.

In addition, the Balkan, Iberian Peninsula, Central Europe, Northern Europe, and Baltic countries also have large communication agencies participating in the "World News Agency Alliance," but I cannot describe them all here.

The Grand Scenery of Shanghai

Interior View of a Beauty Hospital 216

— Wen Zheng

We are now in an era where social openness is advocated by everyone, and the young men and women of Shanghai are particularly at the forefront of this movement. Therefore, the cries of "physical fitness" and "beauty" are flying everywhere. As a result, beauty hospitals have emerged to meet this great need.

The clients of beauty hospitals are not only a large number of women, but also many men who consider themselves unattractive, and enthusiastically seek advice. This is because beauty hospitals don't just do makeup for people; they can also transform faces full of freckles and wrinkles into clean, white, and tender skin, flatten out pockmarks and scars until they are unnoticeable, and do their best to bring out your physical beauty and restore the charm you've lost.

In order to understand the situation of beauty treatments, this reporter recently made a special visit to the Shi's Beauty Hospital. According to the investigation, this beauty hospital is indeed the first of its kind in Shanghai, having been established for five years. It is located in the Women's Bank Building, which is next to the Hongmiao Temple on Nanjing Road. We can see many gorgeously dressed women burning incense and praying at Hongmiao Temple, while at the same time going to the beauty hospital for "treatment," using the help of science to increase their youth and happiness.

When this reporter arrived at the waiting room of the beauty hospital, the staff at the registration desk probably thought I was there for beauty treatments and asked me to register. I explained that I was there for a special visit, so he asked me for a business card and went into the office. I saw a sign hanging at the registration desk that read: "Consultation Hours: 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM, 2:00 PM to 6:00 PM daily. Closed Sunday afternoons." "Registration Fee: $1.60, subsequent visits $0.60 each." After a while, a gentleman in a Western suit came out of the office. He introduced himself as Mr. Tu, in charge of business affairs, and asked what I wanted to see. I said I was there for a special visit. He then went into the consulting room to tell Doctor Shi Shuanghu. Soon, Doctor Shi came out. He was a man in his thirties, with a short beard and glasses, from Fujian. He didn't speak Mandarin very well, but his attitude was very sincere. I paid special attention to his own face, and indeed his skin was moisturized, white, clean, and refreshing, and his clothes were extremely neat. He led me to first observe the consulting room. Although the room was not large, the arrangement was very elegant. A desk was placed in front of the window, and in addition to stationery, there were dozens of small glass bottles and glass containers similar to small wine glasses. It was said that these all contained medicinal products for use. Next to the window was a filing cabinet, which was said to contain newspapers, magazines for reference, and special publications compiled by Mr. Shi himself. The lighting inside was particularly bright, making it extremely clear to see people's faces, which I assumed was for easy facial examination. Next to the consulting room was the electrotherapy room, which was equipped with a sun lamp and a rectangular cabinet-like electrical cabinet. It was said that this was a "hot light" and "quartz lamp" irradiator, which could irradiate the whole body, the face, and be used for electrotherapy on women's flat breasts, etc. It was explained that electrical irradiation could quickly circulate the blood in the body, activate internal cells, and that, in addition to removing wrinkles and spots on the skin with lotions, electric current could also help with their treatment. A specially made leather-padded chair was provided for the patient during electrotherapy, resembling the chairs used in barbershops. Next to it were hot and cold water pipes and a washbasin, and various cosmetics were displayed, such as: Beauty Dew, Almond Honey, Beauty Snow (the above three types are used instead of vanishing cream, but their effects can remove wrinkles, prevent freckles, minimize pores, and provide a foundation that doesn't fade), Beauty Body Fluid (also known as Body Beauty Dew, can prevent skin diseases and keep skin white and tender), Sunscreen Beauty Cream (prevents sunburn), Mouth Fragrance (removes bad breath and protects teeth), Glycerin Soap (non-irritating and alkaline-free, can keep skin white and tender), Depilatory (can remove beards without harming the skin), etc., all made by Mr. Shi himself. The reporter picked up bottle after bottle to look at, try, and ask about their effects. I only felt a fragrant aroma, delicate and smooth, unlike ordinary products. It was said that these kinds of cosmetics sold very well.

According to Dr. Shi, the medical skills of the beauty hospital include the following:

Facial: Removal of freckles, mole removal, removal of various colors (yellow, gray, black, white, red) spots, making rough, dark skin white and tender, turning dark neck skin white, skin whitening injections, removal of facial keratosis, removal of acne, pimples, scars, removal of sores, flattening of pockmarks, removal of facial tumors, removal of facial boils, facial (illegible) removal, etc.

Various Electrotherapies: Facial electrotherapy, body electrotherapy, breast electrotherapy.

Eye and Eyebrow Area: Cataract (blindness) surgery, eyebrow growth, eyebrow reshaping, turning single eyelids into double eyelids, surgery for uneven eyes, enlarging small eyes, eye leakage, inward and outward turning of eyelids, strabismus surgery, (illegible).

Nose Area: Rosacea, stopping excessive nasal oil, red nose removal, rhinoplasty, polyp removal, nasal polyps.

Lip Area: Harelip (cleft lip) closure, narrowing wide mouths, teeth whitening, separating lip adhesions from skin.

Ear Area: Earlobe repair, ear tumors, separating ear adhesions from skin.

Hand and Foot Area: Turning dark and rough skin on upper limbs white and tender, oily gray nails, armpit odor (body odor), itchy toes, corns.

Makeup: Light makeup, heavy makeup, special makeup (electrical makeup), hair loss prevention, hair growth, bald head hair growth, changing fat to thin, changing emaciation to plumpness, chest and breast development injections.

Among these, the flattening of pockmarks is the most troublesome. It is said that if the pockmarks are on good skin and the marks are clearly demarcated, then the procedure is extremely easy, and large pockmarks can be flattened in twenty days. However, if the pockmarks are in clusters and not clearly distinguishable, and the skin is too tight, then it often takes five to six months. Rhinoplasty is also quite troublesome, i.e., turning a flat nose into a high nose bridge, as the saying goes. In the past, beauty doctors mostly used hard wax, which was a bit like a joke, because the result looked like a fake nose, and if you weren't careful, it would collapse again. However, the ivory support method can now be used to remedy this. Also, for the removal of sores, ordinary surgeons mostly cut and then suture the wound, but Dr. Shi invented a method that only requires applying a homemade lotion around the sore, turning the skin in that area into rubber, and then slowly shaving it off with a small knife, so that it naturally heals flat without leaving a mark. The same is true for turning single eyelids into double eyelids; you only need to draw a line with homemade lotion, and that area will naturally separate to form double eyelids. However, this is not applicable to people with excessively upturned eyelids. Mr. Shi studied in Tokyo and later opened a beauty hospital in Singapore. In Shanghai, his most famous surgery is the radical cure of freckles, and he has invented a radical freckle-curing lotion that is extremely effective. After the reporter's visit, I returned to the waiting room and saw three or four fashionable women waiting there for consultation. I shook hands with Dr. Shi to say goodbye and walked out of the hospital door in a burst of fragrant air.

Common Knowledge

The Historical Development of Weapons 217

— Qing Jun

Humans are animals that can use and manufacture tools, and weapons are naturally one of the tools that humans use to conduct life struggles. If the progress of production tools is the manifestation of human evolution, then the evolutionary process of humanity can also be seen in the historical development of weapons.

Weapons can be said to have existed since primitive times. However, the weapons at that time were very immature and crude, and were only used to deal with wild beasts and poisonous snakes, and were not used by humans to kill each other. The appearance of weapons for human warfare occurred after the formation of pastoral and agricultural societies, and after the emergence of private property systems. Because at that time, humans had fixed living areas, had privately owned property, and therefore wars to seize land, property, and slaves occurred.

The earliest weapons can be said to have been made of stone; bronze weapons then appeared; as for the appearance of iron weapons, it was around three thousand years before the Common Era. The first to use iron weapons were the Egyptian infantry. They had spears as long as six feet, shields covered with iron sheets on sturdy wood, and a saber hanging horizontally on their waists. Naturally, there were also bows and arrows at that time, as well as various specialized archers. But the most formidable weapon at that time was an early type of chariot. These chariots were of different weights: light chariots moved farther and were mostly used on general battlefields; heavy chariots could penetrate deep into the enemy's center, directly charging the enemy and inflicting fatal attacks.

After Egypt, what is worth mentioning is of course the weapons of the Greek era. Indeed, around the sixth century before the Common Era, Greece had very organized standing armies, which were mostly composed of infantry. Among this infantry, there was a distinction between heavy infantry and light infantry: the former belonged to the upper ranks, and their weapons were spears, short swords, shields, and armor; the latter belonged to the lower ranks, and they used knives and crossbows as weapons, without protective shields and armor. Horses were already commonly used for combat at this time, but knights could not yet use stirrups, because the appearance of stirrups was five hundred and fifty years after the Common Era. As for the most outstanding weapon at this time, it was the spear, which was more than twenty feet long. When fighting, the so-called spearmen relied on large shields for protection, held twenty-foot-long spears, stood in front of the formation, and charged forward. Alexander, who established unprecedented military achievements in history, actively developed the power of these spears.

Following the Greek era was the Roman era. The typical weapon of this era was a double-edged short sword. The sword was twenty inches long and was suitable for both thrusting and short chopping; this weapon is not known how many people it killed. In addition, darts and spears were also commonly used by warriors in the Roman era. These warriors wore iron helmets, armor, and short swords at their waists, and carried long or short spears, with darts that could be thrown at any time. They were truly awe-inspiring and looked like they wouldn't blink an eye when killing people.

However, history showed the greatest enemy of Rome, which were the Muhammadan believers who "held a sword in their right hand and the Koran in their left hand." They had Chinese-style green dragon crescent blades, as well as short spears, swords, darts, bows and arrows, and other weapons. However, they were fearless of death. They didn't wear helmets or use shields on the battlefield, and they charged straight ahead, which the Romans couldn't resist.

After the fall of the Roman Empire, European society entered the dark period of the Middle Ages, which is the so-called feudal era in social history. The feudal lords of this era all raised many warriors to be loyal to themselves, and thus the famous knights of the Middle Ages appeared.

In order to show their majesty and to win over the hearts of their subordinates, the lords did not hesitate to desperately exploit the peasants, arming their knights in a very mighty and gorgeous manner; according to historical facts, the cost of arming each knight was at least thirty pounds. These knights rode fat horses, wore short swords, and carried long spears and double swords, and they had to fully express their heroic spirit everywhere.

The infantry under the knights mainly used spears, short swords, and shields. In the infantry, there were archers whose arrows could reach seventy to one hundred and fifty yards. This can be said to have been one of the most powerful weapons at that time.

The most famous war of the Middle Ages was undoubtedly the Crusades. In this war, the activity of cavalry occupied a very important position. Both the European cavalry and the Turkish cavalry wore swords, spears, bows, and arrows, but due to the climate, the Turkish cavalry were more lightly armed; at the same time, the swords they used were also slightly different from those of Europe, namely, theirs were curved, while those used by Christian Europe were straight swords.

Due to the repeated Crusades, due to the continuous wars, and due to the development of industry, with the end of the dark period of the Middle Ages, weapons also made leaps and bounds. Taking bows as an example, around the sixteenth century, the old bows (Longbow) gradually became crossbows (Crossbow). The power of this crossbow was several times that of the bow, and it could shoot beyond two hundred and fifty yards without losing its effectiveness.

But the biggest event at this time was the invention of gunpowder and the appearance of artillery. Originally, gunpowder had already existed in China around one thousand years before the Common Era, but Europeans began to use gunpowder for guns and cannons during the Renaissance. What is worth mentioning here is that in 1540, a famous person named Vitelli invented a short gun that was less than two feet long. Although it was not as sophisticated and powerful as modern pistols, it was easy to fire and carry, and it can be said to have been the most modern weapon at the time. As for the appearance of cannons, it was earlier than the invention of this short gun. In the fourteenth century, the German army used cannons to win battles. In the Battle of Constantinople in 1453, Muhammad II also organized an artillery team, using seventy cannons; among them, three had a caliber of twenty-five inches, and could project a stone of one thousand five hundred pounds to a mile away. The Greek army that fought against it can be said to have been defeated by these cannons.

The appearance of such cannons and short guns is worth noting in the history of weapons. Because with these things, especially with the development of these things, the old swords, spears, halberds, etc. would gradually lose their effectiveness in war, and the old martial arts would gradually become historical relics, so the strategy and tactics in war would inevitably change. Based on this point, we can say that the weapons and wars before the appearance of guns and cannons in the sixteenth century were ancient and feudal, and the weapons and wars after that were modern.

In modern history, there have also been many major wars; in these wars, many new and strange weapons have appeared. Now let's briefly examine the weapons of several major eras.

First is the famous Napoleonic era. In this era, the infantry weapons used by Napoleon to disturb all of Europe were rifles and bayonets. It is said that at one point, Napoleon discovered that his soldiers had abandoned their bayonets, so he seriously said to the soldiers: "The bayonet is the best weapon for soldiers, and it is the most suitable weapon for French soldiers. Anyone who loses his bayonet will be severely punished!" When Napoleon commanded the Italian army, he abolished the swords held by the army and replaced them with bayonets. This was because the bayonet could be used with the rifle at the same time, which was more convenient; it could also show great power in hand-to-hand combat.

The army of the Napoleonic era, of course, had complete infantry, cavalry, artillery, and logistics. Among these, apart from the engineers and logistics soldiers who had special tasks, the cavalry's weapons of war were similar to those of the infantry, and the artillery mainly used six-, eight-, and twelve-pound cannons, although there were also sixteen-pound cannons, but the number was very small.

Second is the weapons of the Franco-Prussian War era. Almost many of the most powerful weapons currently used already existed at that time. For example, the rifles used by the French army at that time had an effective shooting range of one thousand three hundred yards. This was of course much more powerful compared to the rifles of the Napoleonic era. As for the cannons used by the artillery, although those used by the French were larger than those used by the Germans, because the French loaded the shells from the muzzle, while the Germans loaded the shells from the breech, the power of the latter actually exceeded that of the former.

In the Franco-Prussian War, German artillery displayed its greatest power. Its artillery formation was: 1. Fifteen steel rifled cannons; 2. Twelve bronze rifled cannons; 3. Nine steel rifled cannons; 4. Fifteen bronze rifled howitzers; 5. Twenty-one cm bronze rifled field guns. Under the power of such an artillery formation, the French army was defeated.

Finally, of course, are the weapons that appeared in the World War that broke out in 1914, which are the well-known airplanes, tanks, poison gas, etc. As for the weapons of future wars, they will certainly be even more powerful, which we will soon see. However, the development of weapons can be said to have reached its peak, so what is its future? We dare to boldly say: it will disappear permanently with the permanent elimination of human mutual national strife.

Lifestyle

Printing Workers 218

— Zhu Yongkang

I have been working in the printing bureau for ten years. I came here as an apprentice when I was thirteen years old, and now I have been promoted to the "imposition" work. In these full ten years of life, I have only been friends with "type". What we see, what we handle, and what we pay attention to are all "type". All day long in this room with not much sunlight and not very well ventilated air, breathing the smell of "ink" and oil smoke. I have long felt that life is too monotonous and too boring, and I really want to change my taste and find another job; but I seem to have become a specialized typesetter, and in this era of unemployment panic, I have to make do.

When I came here ten years ago, people all called me "student boy". The work of the student boy was to "select type" and "return type". Before selecting and returning type, you had to learn the "categories" of Chinese characters. The way to recognize "character collections" was entirely according to the "Kangxi Dictionary". Now, of course, I am very familiar with it. But at that time, I was only at the level of a higher primary school student? There were so many Chinese characters, and the classification was so complicated, that it took me two months of "trial learning" to barely memorize them. But the "radicals" of Chinese characters and "elements" could not always follow the general rules. For example, the character "分" (fēn, divide), do you think it is in the "八" (bā, eight) radical? But it is actually in the "刀" (dāo, knife) radical. And like the "阝" (yì, city) radical and the "阝" (fù, mound) radical, sometimes it is hard to distinguish them clearly. So after two months of trial learning, I only remembered some generally, as for detailed classification, it took at least two years to become familiar with it. "Type" is generally placed obliquely on rows and rows of wooden shelves, and characters with the same radical are placed in the same column. In the same column, characters with fewer strokes are placed in front, and characters with more strokes are placed behind, arranged in the same way as characters in the dictionary. But selecting type is much more difficult than looking up a dictionary. After you select one character, you may have to run several steps to find the second character. Because the arrangement of characters on the "original manuscript" is not arranged according to the order of the dictionary. You run once to select a character, and you run ten times to select ten characters. If you select a thousand characters without rest, your head will already be dizzy, not to mention that you only have the opportunity to stand and run, and you never have the opportunity to sit for a quarter of an hour? I worked as a student boy for three years. I continued to stand for three years and ran for three years in the "type room". Not only were my legs sore and numb, but they also turned yellow and swollen. And my eyes? New type is easy to recognize, but ninety percent of the type has been stained with ink, and in a room with dim sunlight, you have to stare hard to be able to distinguish it.

The selected type you put on the "tray", arranging them row by row according to the order of the original manuscript, ready for others to take away for "imposition". When the form has been made, or has been printed, or has been "paper pasted", this "type form" has to be removed, and the removed type is returned by us student boys, which is called "returning type". Returning type is almost as troublesome as selecting type. Where you picked it up from, you have to run around to return it to its original place, and the order of the character collection must not be confused at all, otherwise it will be even more troublesome to select it the second time.

Selecting type and returning type are the minimum work for us typesetters, but also the hardest work. Our hands are all covered in black ink, so you can't wipe your face or rub your nose, otherwise you'll be covered in ink. You never wear clean clothes all year round. But the wages are extremely pitiful. Generally, ten hours of work a day can earn thirty to forty cents of silver. The number of characters selected and returned in a day is at least four thousand or more. When I get home at night, my legs and feet ache all night long, and my eyes are red and swollen. I still can't recover by the next morning, but I still have to drag my tired body to work.

The apprentice life of selecting type and returning type for three years is considered to be completed. The clever ones can be promoted to "engraving" workers, and the clumsy ones still select type, return type, or "dismantle forms". On the surface, "engraving" is much more comfortable and economical than the first step of work. You can sit still and talk a little cleaner; but engraving those five-point and six-point characters, and using lead for engraving, not only can your eyes not stand it, but you
